Shanghai United One Yuan Support for Suiyuan Association Carries Out Fundraising Work 122

Propaganda Rally Canceled

General Mobilization Still Scheduled for the 20th

The Shanghai First Special District Citizens' United One Yuan Support for Suiyuan Association held its third plenary committee meeting yesterday, attended by over twenty people, including Cao Zhigong. Zhu Shixiang chaired the meeting. The chairman first reported on the previous meeting's decision to hold a propaganda rally to expand the movement. However, since the Xi'an Incident, local order has become extremely important. The question was raised whether it was still necessary to hold this rally and a decision was requested. After discussion, it was decided to cancel the propaganda rally for the sake of prudence. However, the fundraising work is still scheduled for general mobilization on the 20th. It is reported that the association's one-yuan donation books, which were previously submitted to the Bureau of Social Affairs for stamping, were retrieved yesterday and will be distributed to the committee members in the coming days to carry out fundraising in the sub-associations.

Customs Issues Maritime Police Notice; Navigation Difficult in Xunhan Section 123

River Water Recedes to 9 Feet 5 Inches; Difficult for Larger Riverboats to Reach Hankou

The Yangtze River water level has dropped to 9 feet 5 inches yesterday. Riverboats with deeper drafts have been blocked from reaching Hankou. The customs office issued a maritime police notice for the Jiujiang-Hankou section yesterday (the 16th) because a civilian ship ran aground at Honggaopo, making navigation very dangerous. The notice is as follows: Maritime Police Notice (Jiujiang and Hankou Section). Previously, a civilian ship ran aground in the center of the Honggaopo waterway on Huoyanshan. It has now been lightened. The waterway is not yet safe. The shallowest water level in the Honggaopo waterway on Huoyanshan was 3.20 meters (10.5 feet) on the 15th of this month, with the Jiujiang water level marker at 1.31 meters (4.3 feet) at the same time. The shallowest water level in the East Waterway of Daijia Island was 3.50 meters (11.5 feet) on the 15th of this month, with the Hankou water level marker at 0.73 meters (2.4 feet) at the same time. Deputy Inspector of Customs Maritime Affairs, Terry, Acting Inspector, Republic of China, December 16, 1936.

Real Estate Industry Union Petitions for Reduced Land Tax; Yesterday, They Submitted a Petition to the Municipal Government, Explaining the Drastic Drop in Land Values; Requesting the Land Bureau to Reassess Land Values and Reduce Tax Amounts 125

The Shanghai Real Estate Industry Association submitted a petition to the Municipal Government yesterday requesting the Municipal Government to instruct the Land Bureau to reassess land values and reduce land taxes. The petition stated: "Petition for instructing the Land Bureau to reassess land values and reduce tax amounts to alleviate the burden and show sympathy. The land prices in Shanghai have plummeted in recent years due to the decline in commerce and the exhaustion of the market. The real estate industry has suffered the most. As a result of this trend, there have been frequent cases of families going bankrupt. This situation is already well known to the Municipal Government. The land tax is based on the market value assessed by the previous Land Bureau Valuation Committee for collection. It has been many years. Due to the current economic recession, there is no hope of recovery in the short term. Landlords are mostly complying with tenants' requests and voluntarily reducing rents. However, on the other hand, they are still painfully paying the land tax according to the previously assessed amount. This has been the case for a long time. However, it is an economic principle that taxes are derived from rents. Now that land values have clearly plummeted and rents have been generally reduced, it is unfair to continue collecting land taxes according to the previously assessed tax amount. The association has repeatedly received complaints from its members, requesting that the land value be reassessed so that the land tax can be reduced. Therefore, we are submitting this petition to the Municipal Government for review and approval to instruct the Land Bureau to reassess the land value in each district and reduce the tax amount from 1937 onwards, in order to be fair and relieve the difficulties of businesses. We are waiting anxiously for your order." Respectfully submitted to Wu, Mayor of the Shanghai Municipal Government.

City Government Sets Up Free Tap Water for the Poor 127

Limited to One Bucket per Person, No Washing Allowed Nearby

In order to facilitate the poor in obtaining tap water, the municipal government has specially instructed the Bureau of Public Utilities to formulate a draft of the rules for the use of free tap water faucets for the poor in the city. This has been approved by the municipal government under directive number 21590. In addition to publicizing it, the Bureau of Public Utilities is also instructed to install free tap water faucets in the city. Those who use free tap water must be genuinely poor and are only allowed to carry one bucket by hand. Carrying water by two people is not permitted. Taverns, restaurants, cafes, tea houses, fish farms, flower growers, factories, hot water stores, barber shops, and wealthy residences are not allowed to use the water. Furthermore, washing vegetables, rinsing rice, and doing laundry near the faucets is prohibited in order to comply with the regulations.

Customs Brokers and Others Negotiate with Six Companies 128

Refusal of Requests Leads to Suspension of Operations

After six companies, including the state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, the private Sanbei Company, Jiu Shao Company, British-owned Taikoo Company, Jardine Matheson & Co., and Japanese-owned Nissin Steamship Co., announced that water freight charges for various ports along the Yangtze River would be collected according to the weight on the scales, the Shanghai Transportation and Customs Brokers Association and the Shanghai Businessmen's Association jointly opposed this. After a meeting, it was decided that if the companies did not agree to their request, operations would be suspended. The two associations jointly announced: "Regarding the statement by the six shipping companies that, starting from December 15th, all goods transported to various ports along the Yangtze River and charged according to weight will be subject to the rates determined by the Pingzhun Company scales, we have sent numerous letters and delegated representatives to demand the cancellation of the new rule. The six companies have agreed to hold a meeting this Wednesday to discuss the matter. After convening a joint meeting, our association has resolved that, regardless of the outcome of the six companies' discussion, we insist that water freight charges be calculated based on the weight declared to customs for tax purposes. If the companies do not agree to our request, we will have no choice but to suspend operations pending a resolution." Yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM, the six companies held a joint meeting and decided to send representatives to negotiate with the Transportation and Customs Brokers Association and the Shanghai Businessmen's Association to resolve the issue, and agreed to temporarily postpone the implementation of the collection of water freight charges based on the scales for various ports along the Yangtze River.

Robbery on Avenue Haig: One Thief Killed, Two Captured - Guns and Knives Found in Chamber Pots - Stolen Foreign Currency of $390 Recovered 129

Lu Maoyuan, a native of Shaoxing, runs the Yong Tai Mao Ji tobacco and currency exchange shop at 534 Avenue Haig. At around 6:00 AM yesterday morning, while Lu was still fast asleep, four robbers armed with guns and knives arrived to rob the shop. They pried open the door and crept inside. Lu's wife, Mrs. Xi, happened to be coming downstairs in her robe when she was stopped and ordered not to move. The robbers then searched the shop, eventually stealing over 300 yuan in foreign currency before fleeing with the loot. Seeing the robbers leave, Mrs. Xi rushed upstairs and woke up the apprentice, Lu Arong, telling him about the robbery. Upon hearing the news, Lu Arong immediately ran downstairs, chased after the robbers outside the shop, and enlisted the help of two neighbors from a nearby brokerage shop. They saw the four robbers turn south into Jinjiazhai Lane along Avenue Haig and enter No. 2, Lane 762 on Chengdu Road. Lu immediately reported to the patrol, who promptly informed the police station. A large number of Chinese and foreign detectives were dispatched to the scene. Just as they were about to rush into the lane to apprehend the robbers, a shot suddenly rang out from a dark corner of a small alley. The detectives returned fire and bravely charged in, killing one robber on the spot with a bullet to the right side of his head, and seizing a gun. Two robbers were captured alive. After being taken to the police station for interrogation, they identified themselves as Wang Acai, 31 years old, and Tian Linchang, 29 years old, both from Ningbo. The dead robber was identified as Zhou Jiaxiang, 29 years old, from Chaozhou, who lived in an upper room behind a small house in the lane. The detectives then searched the premises again, finding Zhou's mistress, Ms. Li, and her daughter, Gendi. They also found another gun and a knife in a chamber pot, as well as 390 yuan in stolen foreign currency in a chest of drawers. All were taken back to the police station for safekeeping, awaiting submission to the court for investigation and prosecution this morning. The robber's body has been sent to the coroner for examination.

Thunder and Rain Yesterday 130

Heavy Fog in the Morning and Evening - Rare in Winter

Over the past two days, the weather in this city has suddenly turned mild, resembling the climate of spring. There was heavy fog in the morning and evening. Yesterday was even warmer, with the sky sometimes cloudy and sometimes clear, but with dense clouds that did not bring rain. At 8:10 PM, the rain became heavier, lasting for only fifteen minutes. As it rained, lightning flashed and thunder rumbled, which is rare in winter. It rained again at around 9:00 PM.

Baoshan County Hospital Officially Opens 133

Ten o'clock in the morning on the twenty-first

Baoshan County is connected to Shanghai's Hudu and bordered by the sea on three sides, with fresh air and convenient transportation, making it ideal for patients to recuperate. However, previously, there was no hospital of substantial scale. Although there were one or two clinics, due to limited finances and rudimentary equipment, they were almost beyond repair. Starting in the twenty-fifth year, the provincial government proposed establishing county hospitals throughout the province, issuing a general order to all opium suppression bureaus in the province. Any county opium suppression bureau that had not yet established a county hospital was required to begin operations in the twenty-fifth year and to start preparations immediately. Shen Ruohan, the director of the Baoshan County Opium Suppression Bureau, received an appointment order in July of the twenty-fifth year to serve as the chief of the county hospital preparatory office, with instructions to expedite preparations. He selected the site of the existing clinic in the county seat as the hospital site. At the same time, he prepared an estimated budget for start-up costs and operating expenses and submitted it to the county for forwarding to the province. Starting in September, he added an obstetrician and staff and reported the establishment of the hospital that month. Meanwhile, he took over the clinic for renovation and repairs and temporarily established a treatment department at the opium suppression bureau to begin medical work. On November 4, he received an appointment order from the Provincial Department of Civil Affairs, appointing Shen Ruohan as the hospital director and issuing the county hospital seal. On November 25, he received approval for the start-up cost budget. At the same time, the hospital site was also completed, and the purchase of equipment and instruments could be done soon. The opening ceremony is now scheduled for December 21. From then on, the health of the entire county will be protected. Not only are the people of the county overjoyed, but patients from Shanghai who wish to be admitted to the hospital can reach the hospital in a few tens of minutes for a peaceful recuperation.

Journalists' Union to Hold General Meeting 134

Submitting a Request for Party and Government Authorities to Send Representatives for Guidance

Gathering for Dinner, Entertainment, and Drawing of Books, Paintings, and Items

The Shanghai News Journalists' Union, in accordance with its constitution, has scheduled its fifth autumn members' general meeting for 4:00 PM on the twentieth of this month, to be held at the Zhengyi Society on the seventh floor of the Continental Emporium. The meeting will include reports on union affairs, discussions of proposals, as well as dinner and entertainment. In keeping with past practice, famous paintings and calligraphy and domestically produced goods will be collected to be raffled off to attending members for entertainment and to add to the enjoyment. The union has submitted a request to party and government authorities to send representatives to attend and provide guidance. Preparations for the meeting are largely complete. Regarding the solicitation of paintings, calligraphy, and entertainment, the union's fourth joint meeting of executive and supervisory committee members previously designated Li Haoran, Jiang Zongdao, Guo Butao, and Hang Shijun to solicit paintings and calligraphy; Sun Daosheng, Ma Zhishan, Zhu Xuefan, and Ma Chonggan to solicit domestically produced goods; and Yan Duhe, Ma Zhishan, and Zhu Mingxin to arrange entertainment. It is now reported that the union has received the following domestically produced goods: twelve pairs of Double Coin brand men's galoshes, twelve Double Coin brand hot water bottles, twelve Double Coin brand student aviator caps, and two hundred and eighty Double Coin brand twenty-four-inch balloons from the Great China Rubber Factory; two dozen large-sized soft-jar cold creams and two dozen Invincible brand toothpastes from the Family Industries Society; twelve bottles of wine; three 404 tumbler insert locks from the Kang Yuan Canning Factory via the China National Products Sales Association; twenty-four boxes of facial makeup and sixty-eight toys; four dozen No. 2 White Jade toothpastes from the China Chemical Industry Society; two hundred sets of exquisite calendars from the Yapu'er Electric Appliance Factory; two hundred and fifty scenic blotting papers from the Zhenhua Paint Company; six hygiene shirts from the Wuhe Weaving Factory; fifty packages of delicious candies from the China Food Company; half a dozen bottles of Lion and Horse brand beef extract from the Stanic Pharmaceutical Factory; two dozen pure steel knives and one electric iron from the Huasheng Electric Appliance Factory; and six diary voucher tickets. More domestically produced goods are being donated by various national goods manufacturers. As for entertainment, the union has obtained the consent of the famous Pingju opera artist Zhu Baoxia to perform famous plays at the meeting and the famous Sutan artist Zhu Guoliang to sing improved Sutan.

German Engineer Zhao Jiewen Returns to China 137

Zhao Jiewen, a native of Wujin, Jiangsu, graduated from Suzhou Industrial School in Jiangsu Province and studied in Germany for over seven years. He interned at the "Vone" Machine Factory and the "Oubao" Electric Factory in Berlin, gaining extensive experience. He then entered the Bochum Industrial University, where he focused on ordinary mechanical engineering and also studied military telecommunications machinery. He earned a German chartered engineer's degree and graduated earlier this month, returning to Shanghai via the Siberian land route. At a time when domestic industry is just beginning and military tensions in North China are rising, it is precisely the time for Zhao to dedicate himself to serving the nation and society.

On December 24, he will leave England aboard the Chichibu Maru, a postal ship departing from San Francisco. After staying in Japan for two months, he will perform in Shanghai, Hong Kong, Manila, Singapore, South Australia, and other places.

Trial of Tang Youren Assassination Case Continues Yesterday; Police Request Court to Extend Investigation by Two Weeks Due to Unfinished Procedures 139

Tang Youren, former Director of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Ministry of Transportation, a native of Hunan, was assassinated on December 25 of last year in front of his private residence, Gan Village, on Rue Gaston in the French Concession. The Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau and the French Concession Police have successively apprehended the perpetrators of the case, Liu Zhennan and Qiu Jiyu. They were brought back by the French police, escorted to the Special No. 2 Court for interrogation and detention, and the case was adjourned for further questioning. This has been reported in this newspaper. At 10:00 AM yesterday, the scheduled continuation of the trial took place. The French police escorted the two defendants, Liu and Qiu, to the criminal division of the Special No. 2 Court, where Criminal Judge Wang Gangxu, accompanied by Clerk Gao Yanmao, took the bench for questioning. According to Fei Xizhen, the lawyer for the police department, the police department's investigation of the case has not yet been completed, and a request was made for a two-week extension to complete the investigation procedures before filing a lawsuit for trial. The court questioned the defendants. Liu confessed to firing one shot, and Qiu admitted to firing four or five shots. At the time, they and the fugitives Yang Yousheng, Xiao Kaihui, and Xiang Xingchang and others, a total of five people, carried out the assassination together. "We have now confessed, so what else is there to investigate?" They also said that they were treated poorly in the police station, with insufficient food, and requested to be transferred to the detention center. The court reviewed the confessions, instructed that the case be adjourned until the thirtieth for further questioning, and ruled that the defendants could not be transferred to the detention center while the case was still under investigation, so they were returned to the police station.

Gu Zhuxuan's Bail Procedures Not Yet Completed; Expected to Regain Freedom Today or Tomorrow 140

Gu Zhuxuan, a native of Yancheng, was involved in the case of instigating the assassination of Tang Jiapeng, as well as the case of bribing guards to buy off inmates Zhao Guangfu and Zhang Tinggui to recant their testimony and fabricate false evidence. The murder case is currently under third instance appeal at the Supreme Court, and the case of instigating false evidence is still under trial at the Special No. 2 Court. Gu has submitted petitions to both the Supreme Court and the Special No. 2 Court requesting bail and suspension of detention. The Special No. 2 Court ruled that he should find two reputable shopkeepers to provide a written guarantee of 20,000 yuan, guaranteeing his presence whenever summoned, and allowing the suspension of detention. The Third Branch of the High Court also convened a court session the day before yesterday afternoon, ruling that he should provide a cash guarantee of 7,000 yuan, plus two reputable shopkeepers to provide a written guarantee of 10,000 yuan, guaranteeing his presence whenever summoned, and allowing the suspension of detention. These details were reported in yesterday's newspaper. It is now learned that Gu's family has been searching for shopkeepers to act as guarantors for days, and has persuaded the owners of the Wanchang Rice Shop and the Xingxinchi Bathhouse to provide a written guarantee of 20,000 yuan. After submitting the guarantee to the court and having the police verify it, at around 3:00 PM yesterday, Judge Chen summoned the two guarantors in the Sixth Tribunal, approved their guarantee for Gu Zhuxuan's release. Regarding the Second Branch of the High Court, Gu's family persuaded the owners of two factories to provide a written guarantee of 10,000 yuan, and submitted shares of the Great World Company to the court as cash. After investigation, the court returned the shares and instructed them to submit other securities or cash. As a result, these procedures could not be completed yesterday afternoon and must be done again today. Gu's family, wives, relatives, and friends, such as Zheng Jianyi, Zhao Ruquan, Zhao Junyu, Ma Honggen, lawyer Wang Jishi, and lawyer Wu Lun, waited until 5:00 PM, intending to welcome Gu Zhuxuan home, but when the court bell rang signaling the end of the day, the bail procedures had not yet been completed. Gu could not be released, so they all dispersed. It is estimated that Gu will regain his freedom today or tomorrow.

Ding Huikang Lectures on "Disease Insurance and National Health" at the Anti-Tuberculosis Exhibition Yesterday 145

The Shanghai Anti-Tuberculosis Exhibition invited Dr. Ding Huikang to lecture yesterday on "Disease Insurance and National Health." His speech was insightful and incisive, and excerpts are as follows:

The Meaning of Disease Insurance

As society progresses, human affairs become more complex, and people are more susceptible to illness. The burden of medical expenses also increases. For the average family, it is not difficult to accurately budget various income and expenditure items, but medical expenses are difficult to predict. The onset of illness is unexpected, and the need for medical care often depletes several years' savings. This is true even for those who are financially capable. Those who are economically disadvantaged and unable to seek medical care are even more numerous. This is the reason for the prevalence of disease insurance organizations in various countries. Therefore, the average family treats disease insurance premiums as a necessary expense. By paying a small monthly fee, they can avoid unpredictable medical expenses and protect the health and well-being of individuals and families through medical security. There is no better way. It is a pity that our country does not yet have such an organization.

Insurance Situation in Various Countries

Disease insurance organizations are divided into two types: public and private. Public disease insurance began in 1871. Those insured are workers, and the premiums paid do not exceed 300 gold. In Germany, for example, there are approximately 20 million insured persons, paying more than 1.2 billion marks annually. In America, it reaches 360 million yuan, and in Russia, it is 250 million rubles. The development of medicine relies entirely on this type of organization for active construction and success. This type of insurance is compulsory, so store owners or managers have a reporting obligation. The expenses are generally borne one-third by the store owner or company and two-thirds by the employees. The premium is approximately 4% to 7% of the monthly salary.

Public Disease Insurance

Public disease insurance is entirely for the benefit of salaried workers. For example, hospital rooms are limited to ordinary third-class wards, and prescriptions cannot be used to purchase prepared medicines. All doctors are divided into treatment areas, and each doctor has a set limit on the number of patients they should treat. The insurance organization then allocates 17% or 20% of its total income annually for doctors' treatment fees. Hospital expenses are also limited. For example, in hospitals in Hamburg, the daily fee is 6.8 marks, including various surgeries, X-rays, and medical expenses. Those insured under this type of insurance are entitled to disease benefits when they are ill, meaning that if the head of a family is hospitalized due to illness, in addition to medical expenses, their family can also receive living expenses.

Private Disease Insurance

Private disease insurance differs from public insurance in that it is not tied to specific doctors. Insured individuals can invite their private physicians for treatment, pay the doctors or hospitals themselves, and then claim reimbursement from the insurance organization.

We Should Catch Up Quickly

In our country now, most doctors do not have a fixed income, and patients are unable to afford medical care. Doctors act independently, without a unified and cooperative approach. Not only does medicine not advance, but it also affects the degeneration of the nation. Observing that medical progress in various countries is directly proportional to the health of their citizens, our country should quickly catch up with this type of disease insurance organization and seek to establish such an insurance organization soon. If the whole country responds enthusiastically, then the day when insurance is popularized will be the day when our country's anti-tuberculosis efforts and medical construction succeed.

Court Sternly Interrogates Cai Fufu and Witnesses in the Wang Jindi Sudden Death Case; Cai's Concubine Dies in Chen Xinglin's Home; Spectator Urged to Wait to Urinate; Court Clerk Detained for Preventing Witness Collusion 146

Cai Fufu, also known as Cai Xuzhou, a local Shanghai resident, operated the Mingyuelou Teahouse on Xiaoshabo Road and Baima Road and also engaged in real estate. He was over forty years old, but he was fond of women. He had previously enticed Wang Ye'gen's daughter, Jindi, who lived at 20 Caishi Lane, Rue Robert, because she often went to Mingyuelou to watch Tanhuang opera. Cai coveted her, used every means to court her, and designed to seduce her. Jindi was deceived and, on April 11 of this year, was invited out by Cai and taken to Room 36 of the Hongxiang Hotel on Avenue Haig. Cai raped Jindi. Unexpectedly, the matter was discovered by Jindi's parents, who went to catch them in the act and apprehended both of them. Later, after Cai repeatedly pleaded, the matter was not reported to the police station. Cai paid a sum of money to cover up the scandal. Who knew that on May 11, Jindi suddenly disappeared again. At the time, Jindi's parents knew that Cai was not without suspicion, but because they could not determine where their daughter was hidden, they temporarily endured and secretly investigated, but after several months, it was like a stone sinking into the sea, with no news at all. Until November 16 of this year, Jindi's uncle, Chen Xinglin, suddenly went to Wang Ye'gen's home with a message, claiming that Jindi had died suddenly in his home. Wang and Chen had rarely visited each other due to disagreements. Upon hearing the bad news, Wang was overcome with grief. After arguing with Chen, Chen revealed that Jindi had been hidden in his home for a long time, initially sent by Cai Fufu. At that time, Jindi appeared to be ill, reportedly caused by Cai's drunken misconduct. Cai also knew that Chen and Wang Ye'gen were not on good terms, so he hid Jindi in Chen's place, assuming that it would not be leaked. Unexpectedly, Jindi fell ill and died. Unable to hide the matter any longer, he informed Wang Ye'gen's wife. Wang Ye'gen, believing that his daughter's death was unclear, rushed to report to the Caojiadu Public Security Sub-Bureau and petitioned the local court for an autopsy. He also filed a criminal self-accusation with the local court, accusing Chen Xinglin and his wife and Cai Fufu of obstructing family affairs. After the court approved the petition, several trials have been conducted. It is learned that the case was reopened at 9:00 AM yesterday in the Criminal Division of the District Court by Judge Wang Shanxiang. The plaintiff, Wang Ye'gen, was detained in the First Special District Court due to a debt dispute and was not present. His lawyer, Qu Cheng, appeared in court. However, Judge Wang stated that Lawyer Qu had not yet submitted his power of attorney to the court and could not appear in court according to law, so he was dismissed as a spectator. He then immediately summoned the defendants and witnesses to state their names and ages, and ordered them all to leave the courtroom for separate questioning. First, Cai Fufu was questioned about the abduction of Wang Jindi. Cai claimed that Jindi was his concubine and that matchmakers Yin Jubao, Cai Futang's wife, and Yao Gengsheng and his wife had acted as intermediaries. After Judge Wang obtained the testimony, he continued to ask detailed questions. After Cai finished testifying, he ordered the court clerk to summon the witness Yao Gengsheng and others. Unexpectedly, at this time, a person in the audience stood up to leave, saying that he needed to urinate. Judge Wang, believing that the case was of great importance and fearing that someone would collude, quickly stopped him and ordered him to wait until all the witnesses were brought to the courtroom before being released. Before the court's instructions were completed, Judge Wang caught a glimpse of the witnesses Yao Gengsheng and others listening outside the courtroom door. Judge Wang believed that the court clerk was derelict in his duty and immediately announced that the trial would be temporarily suspended. He asked the court clerk in the courtroom to invite the chief court clerk to the court and informed him of what had happened. The chief court clerk believed that the court clerk was suspected of colluding with the defendants and witnesses and ordered his temporary detention. Judge Wang then resumed the proceedings and continued to question the witnesses. He had not finished questioning them by noon, so he ruled that the case would be adjourned for retrial.

Around ten o'clock on the morning of the 12th of this month, he filled out the Industrial Bank check for 2,000 yuan to withdraw money, but was unsuccessful because the seal was blurred. He immediately changed his plan and used a Guoxin Bank check, still filling it out for 2,000 yuan. At nine o'clock on the morning of the day before yesterday, when he went to the bank at No. 422 Hankou Road to withdraw the money, he was discovered by the manager of the Meicheng Printing Shop, who reported the situation to the Jiaxing Road police station. The police station sent Chinese detective Jin Yangwu to arrest the tea boy Dong and bring him back to the police station along with the filled-out check and two seals. He was taken into custody. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Third Criminal Division of the First Special District Court. The Municipal Council lawyer, Zhang Shizhu, explained the case and requested prosecution. Afterwards, Wu Zhongxian, the Shaoxing native manager of the Meicheng Printing Shop, and detective Jin reported the process of investigation. They presented the evidence for inspection. When questioned, the tea boy Dong admitted everything. Judge Xiao Xiefen sentenced Dong Huichun to two years imprisonment. The forged check was confiscated and the two seals were returned.

Shanghai People's Hearts Slightly Settled: Trading Market Stable: Flour Margin Reduced, Miscellaneous Grains Subject to Special Margin, Unified Bonds Yesterday Fell by About One Yuan 159

The Shanghai market, as the people's hearts slightly calmed, the trading market has become more stable. Flour margins have been reduced, and miscellaneous grains are subject to special margins. The details are as follows:

Flour Market Firm: Margin Reduced

The Flour Exchange previously announced that for transactions of 1,000 bags, a margin of 1,000 yuan was required because the market price fluctuated too much. Miscellaneous Grains Subject to Special Security Deposit

Yesterday's market conditions at the Miscellaneous Grains Exchange: wheat fluctuated by 0.03-0.04 yuan, sesame seeds rose by 0.50 yuan, soybean oil rose or fell by 0.20-0.30 yuan, soybean cake rose slightly, and soybeans rose by about 0.20 yuan. At the same time, the Exchange issued the following announcements yesterday: (1) Announcement No. 108: In view of the high price of sesame seeds, the small quantity of units, and fluctuations of only 0.20 yuan, it is deemed insufficient. It is hereby decided that starting today, sesame seed fluctuations may not exceed 0.50 yuan. If the limit is exceeded, trading will be stopped and transactions will not be recorded. This is hereby announced. (2) Announcement No. 109: In view of the recent increase in the market prices of various commodities, in order to ensure the stability of both buyers and sellers, in accordance with Article 39, Paragraph 3 of the Business Rules, starting today, a special security deposit of 300 yuan in national currency will be charged to both buyers and sellers for each unit of wheat, soybeans, sesame seeds, and soybean oil, for a total security deposit of 600 yuan. A special security deposit of 200 yuan in national currency will be charged for each unit of soybean oil, for a total security deposit of 400 yuan. This is hereby announced.

Central Bank Inspection Report 160

Central Bank Convertible Note Issuance Reserve 313th Inspection Report: In accordance with Article 13 of the Central Bank Law, the Association is responsible for inspecting the amount of convertible notes issued by the Bank and its reserves. The 313th inspection was held at the Bank's Issuance Bureau on December 12, 1936. The results of the inspection are reported as follows: (A) The total amount of convertible notes issued is 317,047,765 yuan in silver, including 278,015,257 yuan in silver yuan notes and 39,032,508 yuan in subsidiary currency notes. The total amount of convertible note reserves is 317,047,765 yuan, including 207,132,065 yuan in cash reserves in silver. This cash reserve includes 94,519,465.48 yuan stored in the Bank's issuance headquarters, branches, and sub-branches, and 112,612,599.52 yuan deposited with other banks. The security reserve is equivalent to 109,915,700 yuan in silver. (B) The total amount of customs gold convertible notes issued is 400,963.07 yuan. The total amount of customs gold convertible note reserves is 400,963.07 yuan. This reserve includes 7,926.290 ounces of pure gold, priced at 516.8, equivalent to 400,963.07 yuan in customs gold. According to Article 22 of the Central Bank, the cash reserve must be at least 60%, with the remainder guaranteed by legal collateral. The results of this inspection show that the cash reserve exceeds 60% and the security reserve is within 40%, which is in compliance with the regulations. This report is specially submitted. December 14, 1936, Central Bank Board of Supervisors Chairman Li Fusun, Supervisors Xie Mengjun, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Xu Jiqing.

This Year's National Athletic Federation Women's Basketball Championship Canceled 167

Chongde and Qixiu Schedule Exhibition Match

Only Aikoku, Qixiu, and Chongde participated in this year’s National Athletic Federation Women's Basketball Championship. It was originally scheduled to begin on the first of this month, but was postponed because Aikoku was preparing for its 25th anniversary celebration. Yesterday, Mr. Chen Bing-de told reporters that Aikoku had already requested to withdraw from this year's competition. Therefore, only Qixiu and Chongde remain to compete. According to the association's regulations, a championship will not be held if only two schools participate, and the competition will instead be an exhibition match. Therefore, this year's competition between Chongde and Qixiu will follow the precedent and be an exhibition match. However, the date has not yet been determined and will likely be after the Tiecheng Cup basketball tournament concludes.

Charity Basketball Game Yesterday: Zhong Qing Defeats USS Luzon 169

75-41

The Shanghai YMCA held its annual charity basketball game at 7:30 PM last night in the YMCA gymnasium on Sichuan Road to raise funds for the Christmas children's party as usual. It was decided to approve the selection of the above athletes and they are scheduled to depart on February 15th.

Initially, General Takeshita Isamu was recommended as chairman, but Takeshita declined due to his busy schedule. It was decided to ask Vice-Chairman Hiranuma to assume the position of chairman, but Hiranuma also declined. As a result, Lieutenant General Oshima Matayan was nominated and agreed to the position. The association immediately announced the decision regarding the chairman.

Education News

Cultural Circles Unanimously Urge Zhang to Escort Chiang Kai-shek Back to Nanjing 179

Soochow University: Soochow University issued a telegram stating: "Recently, the border wars have been progressing, and it is hoped that the country's power can be strengthened and the national crisis can be alleviated. The whole country should unite as one to demonstrate the true strength of the nation. Unexpectedly, changes have occurred in Xi'an in recent days, holding the commander-in-chief hostage and claiming troops without authorization, inciting internal strife and benefiting external enemies. Even the most foolish person would not be so misguided. Our colleagues at the school are filled with righteous indignation and deep pain. Considering that forbearance is enough to serve the country and that division will lead to destruction, in addition to telegraphing the National Government to launch a swift attack, we respectfully request that all circles unanimously condemn this act to preserve the nation's lifeline and avert national peril. We earnestly hope for this. All faculty, staff, and students of Jiangsu Private Soochow University and Soochow High School respectfully kowtow."

Universities in Zhejiang Province: Zhejiang University and other schools telegraphed Zhang Xueliang, urging him to escort Chairman Chiang Kai-shek back to Nanjing immediately, stating: "Addressed to all newspaper offices nationwide: We recently sent a telegram to Mr. Zhang Aoqing of Xi'an, which stated: 'Chiang Kai-shek is the mainstay of the nation, and the people rely on him. Recently, we heard that you detained him in western Shaanxi, causing shock throughout the country, and rumors are rampant, making it difficult to fathom. We believe that you, having served at home and abroad for a long time and managed military affairs, must share the desire to save the nation, which is facing great difficulties. How can you gamble the nation's fate on a single throw? At a time when the entire country is celebrating unification and the government's measures are in line with public sentiment, and the victory in Suiyuan is widely praised, all actions should be carefully considered in light of the people's wishes and the current environment. Do not be swayed by momentary emotions and be forever condemned by the nation and future generations. We hope that you will exercise your wisdom, pull back from the brink, and immediately escort Chairman Chiang Kai-shek back to Nanjing to preserve the nation's lifeline and avoid becoming a sinner of the Republic of China. We urge you to consider this carefully. With urgent telegrams, we await your instructions.' National Zhejiang University, National College of Art, and Jiangnan College of Liberal Arts and Zhejiang Provincial School of Medicine respectfully express their concern."

China Education Society: The China Education Society telegraphed Zhang Xueliang, stating: "To Mr. Zhang Hanqing of Xi'an: News reports indicate that you used troops to hold Chairman Chiang Kai-shek hostage and made unwarranted demands. At a time when unification has just been achieved and the country is urgently facing incursions from bandits, it is necessary for the whole country to be of one mind and pool resources to resist the enemy and defend the country to strengthen national prestige. Chairman Chiang has dedicated himself to the safety of the nation, spending years running around and planning meritorious deeds. Unexpectedly, you mistakenly believed in conspiracies and harbored malicious intentions, causing this extraordinary change, creating chaos, and shaking the foundation of the nation. Even if personal success or failure is not worth mentioning, what about the credibility of our Chinese nation? No national affairs can be more reckless and absurd than this. We urge you to take a broad view and consider carefully, placing the lives of the entire nation above all else, change your plans immediately, and send capable personnel to escort Chairman Chiang Kai-shek back to Nanjing to preside over the central government's plans. All demands can be presented, and the masses will follow or reject them. This is where the interests of the nation and the people lie. We hope you will handle this well. China Education Society respectfully urges."

Letter from the Shanghai Branch of the Central News Agency: "To Whom It May Concern: In this month's 14th local news report, 'Presidents of Major Middle Schools Telegraph Central Government to Quell Shaanxi Incident,' the name 'He Shi-zhen' was omitted from the list of university presidents in Shanghai. Please include it in the correction column. Shanghai Branch of the Central News Agency, December 16th."

Hubei Province's Literacy Campaign Implements Six-Year Plan, Establishing 70,000 People's Schools to Educate Over 20 Million Illiterates, Adopting Tutorial System and Civic Training Outside of People's Schools 180

Wuhan Correspondence: Education in Hubei Province is backward, and it is even more difficult to popularize in rural areas. According to government statistics, among the province's over 30 million people, there are more than 17 million and 76 thousand and 4353 illiterates, and in reality, the number is definitely higher. Implementing universal education is intended for the entire population, with the purpose of training the general public in the ethics and discipline that should be followed in public and private life, and providing the knowledge and skills necessary for daily life. The meaning is very important. However, because the age of the educated varies, the teaching methods are different, so there are divisions of compulsory education, literacy education, and civic training. In order to complete universal education, the Department of Education has decided to implement a supplementary education plan for out-of-school people starting this year, to eliminate illiteracy in the province within six years. The main points are to organize a provincial universal education committee as the general organization for promoting and implementing supplementary education for out-of-school people in the province. The provincial capital and various counties and cities will also form sub-committees. The methods are: (1) To widely establish people's schools. All out-of-school people who exceed the age of compulsory education must enter people's schools for supplementary education. However, priority should be given to men and women aged sixteen to thirty-five, and then extended to older and younger people. (2) Adopt a tutorial system. The tutorial system should continue to be promoted in areas where it has been effective to supplement what people's schools cannot cover. (3) Implement civic training. It should be promoted first in the provincial capital and prosperous towns, and every Sunday should be designated as training time. The implementation of the above three methods should strive for mutual connection. Regarding people's schools, there are two types: single-established and affiliated. Single-established people's schools adopt a half-day, two-part system, with each school having two classes. Affiliated people's schools belong to organizations and groups, each with one or two classes; those belonging to schools have one class for every two existing grades, and those with only one class must also add a class. Each class is limited to 50 students. Single-established schools have three hours of teaching per day, or two hours. Affiliated schools have two hours of teaching per day. Those established in rural areas should avoid the farming season. The length of study, calculated by the amount of teaching time, should not be less than 200 hours. The provincial capital and various counties and cities take the Bao-Jia area as the unit for implementing supplementary education for out-of-school people, to be completed in phases from August of the 15th year of the Republic of China (1926) to July of the 21st year of the Republic of China (1932). In the first year (August of the 25th year to July of the 26th year), the city of Hankou will establish 400 classes of people's schools, the provincial capital will establish 120 classes of people's schools, and the counties will establish a total of 4,200 classes of people's schools. In the second year (August of the 26th year to July of the 27th year), the city of Hankou will establish 600 classes of people's schools, the provincial capital will establish 200 classes of people's schools, and the counties will establish a total of 7,000 classes of people's schools. In the third year (August of the 27th year to July of the 28th year), the city of Hankou will establish 800 classes of people's schools, the provincial capital will establish 280 classes of people's schools, and the counties will establish a total of 9,800 classes of people's schools. In the fourth year (August of the 28th year to July of the 29th year), the city of Hankou will establish 1,000 classes of people's schools, the provincial capital will establish 360 classes of people's schools, and the counties will establish 12,600 classes of people's schools. In the fifth year (August of the 29th year to July of the 30th year), the city of Hankou will establish 1,200 classes of people's schools, the provincial capital will establish 440 classes of people's schools, and the counties will establish 15,400 classes of people's schools. In the sixth year (August of the 30th year to July of the 21st year), the city of Hankou will establish 1,400 classes of people's schools, the provincial capital will establish 520 classes of people's schools, and the counties will establish 74,520 classes of people's schools. Each class will run at least two terms per year. Together with the students of the tutorial and vocational education programs, over 800,000 people can be taught. At the same time, people with better achievements in universal education will be required to take on the role of teaching. It is expected that the illiteracy of the province will gradually be eliminated within the six-year period.

He has specialized in the church law of the European Middle Ages, and church law, together with Roman law, is the mother law of the continental legal system. Investigation: Shanghai Commodity Price Index Rises 206

November, Year 25

According to the report of the National Tariff Hsiu-jih Association, in November of the 25th year, the Shanghai wholesale, export, and import commodity price indices, as well as the cost of living index, all rose compared to the previous month. The wholesale price increase was particularly high. (Cotton yarn, cotton cloth, wheat, and flour) all continued to rise in price due to brisk sales. (Raw silk, hardware) saw domestic selling prices rise in unison due to sharp increases overseas. This is the main reason for the rise in the index. The details are explained below:

Wholesale Commodity Price Index: The overall index was 113.0, an increase of 3.0% compared to July and 9.4% compared to the same month last year. All eight sub-indices showed increases compared to the previous month. The largest increase was in the (metals, building materials, pharmaceuticals, and textiles) category. The remaining categories did not exceed 2%. The metals category rose by 6.9%. Among the various items, except for (tinplate, black iron pipes, and sewing needles), which remained stable, all others rose. The most notable increase was in lead bars, which rose by 24%, due to recent price increases overseas and scarce inventory. The pharmaceuticals category rose by 5.3%. Douglas fir prices increased due to the American seamen's strike, which hindered supply. (Lime, black bricks, cement, and China fir) also rose by 7% to 14%. Textiles rose by 4.6%. Cotton cloth prices continued to rise due to strong sales, with printed calico rising by 20% and (fine cloth, fine twill, cotton drill) rising by more than 10%. Cotton yarn prices rose by 7% to 10%, reaching the highest price since the second half of the year, due to large purchases from "Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Tianjin, and Guangdong," and spinning mills were working overtime, yet supply still could not meet demand, and local Japanese factories also experienced a labor strike at this time. However, cotton prices remained stable at the same time, and the cotton spinning industry, which had been in difficulty for a long time, showed signs of turning around, with yarn prices high and cotton prices low. In other instances, dried cocoons rose sharply due to extreme scarcity of spot goods, and white silk rose sharply due to external markets. (Woolen cloth, velvet, silk, satin) markets were also firm.

Export Commodity Price Index: The overall index was 97.1, an increase of 1.0% compared to the previous month and 8.4% compared to the same month last year. All three sub-indices showed increases compared to July. Raw materials increased more, while consumer goods and raw material products increased less. Raw materials increased by 2.5%. White silk prices rose sharply in unison in European and American markets. According to the New York price of Shanghai white silk on the 14th of this month compared to the 15th of last month, the price per pound rose from US$1.63 to US$1.83. The trend in the French and British silk markets was the same. Furthermore, the price of cocoons rose sharply due to the poor autumn cocoon harvest domestically, and costs increased, and the local selling price per dan rose from 740 yuan last month to 830 yuan this month. Cotton yarn and asphalt prices also tended to rise. However, tung oil prices fell as new supplies gradually increased, sales of raw oil were sluggish, and soybean oil prices declined in the Lian market. Otherwise, the rate of increase in this category would not have been limited to this. Consumer goods rose by 1.0%. Hog fat prices rose sharply due to shortages. Egg prices were firm and rising, along with coarse cloth and flour, etc. Raw material products rose by 0.4%. Pig iron, pure antimony, and dried cocoons rose by more than 10% due to shortages of inventory, and tin ingots rose due to overseas price increases. Hog bristles, waste silk, and China fir all rose. As a result, the animal products, forestry products, and mineral products indices in this category all rose. However, the abundant production of soybeans, a major export, fell along with the Lian market, and raw kernels arrived in abundance, with sluggish sales, and green beans and cottonseed cake also tended to fall, so the index was lower than the previous month, and the rising trend of the raw material products index was also softened as a result. (To be continued)
