Waistcoat Woolen Overcoats Still in Vogue 207

Woolen overcoats, especially those with lining, are most popular. They are not only light and easy to wear, but also last a long time. Therefore, most men's overcoats nowadays abandon thick wool and are made with lining. This trend has been prevalent for twelve or thirteen years. At that time, the material used was riding breeches wool, with No. 1005 being the best. Initially, it sold for eight taels and five qian of silver per yard. Later, the supply increased annually, and No. 2 and No. 3 goods were imported. Japanese goods were also spun, flooding the Chinese market. Western clothing stores in the Da Xin Street area resumed advertising, and the sales of riding breeches woolen overcoats became increasingly prosperous. Later, due to too many orders for No. 1005, and inconsistent quality, Kong Shi Foreign Firm changed it to No. 100. Other merchants changed it to No. 1009. As a result, the good ones are now called "Old No. 1005," and the inferior ones are called "New No. 1005." After the abolition of the tael and the adoption of the yuan, domestic Zhanghua products were produced, and imports of both domestic and foreign goods continued to increase, causing prices to gradually decline with the environment. By 1931, customers had largely become tired of riding breeches woolen overcoats. Keqiding suddenly rose in popularity, but still could not replace them. Last year, Zhan Luoding lined overcoats became newly popular, and this year even more so, but they are still difficult to defeat riding breeches wool, because most Keqiding are Japanese goods, and the price is difficult to reduce, but they lose their shape quickly after wearing. Furthermore, Ding tends to shed gray fuzz, while riding breeches wool does not have the above-mentioned common problems, so it has always been popular. The domestic Zhanghua brand’s Yihe riding breeches wool is suitable, with low prices and cheaper imports, and the quality is also solid.

Silk and Tea Overseas Silk Prices Rise Local Raw Silk Sales Gradually Open 208

Yesterday, the overseas silk market was relatively stable. New York and Lyon silk prices remained at the previous day's levels. New York spot prices rose by one point, and futures rose by three and a half points. Yokohama spot and futures each rose by ten yuan. The market sentiment was quite strong for a time. Shanghai's silk market is also gradually opening up for sales. White Factory B-grade 20/22 strips sold for 725 yuan yesterday, showing considerable improvement compared to the previous day. In terms of users, only Hangzhou merchants traded, and prices also rose slightly, but unfortunately, there were not many transactions.

Red and Green Tea Domestic Sales Slightly Active 209

Recently, the tea market has been very sluggish for foreign firms. European and American firms believe that the goods on the market are scarce and do not meet sales tastes. In addition, the winter solstice is approaching, so they are mostly taking a wait-and-see attitude. However, domestic sales of fine Xiu Mei and Fu Xi grades have gradually improved. Gangdong, Guangdong and Shantou merchants are rushing to purchase 700-odd boxes in Shanghai daily, with prices opening at twelve or thirteen yuan. It is reported that the Wulong black tea from old Jia Tai Yu Xin Long and other tea houses has shipped four or five hundred boxes due to replenishment messages from Tianjin.

Sugar Market New Tide Green Continues to Fall by Four or Five Jiao 210

Yesterday, the sugar market trend was stable. The association's benchmark price for 24 coarse sand white spot goods was 21 yuan and 6 jiao. The transshipment of high-quality goods was 6 yuan and 2 jiao and 2 fen, with transactions already made. Among the Dongbai, only the spot goods of the SH mark were priced at 21 yuan and 2 jiao and a half, and were also allocated. The remaining items lack further news. The staple cotton red silk remained unchanged. The Hao grade goods had Chaozhou merchants selling over a hundred packages of new tide , but the selling was slack. In addition, sales in the north were sluggish, and suddenly fell by four or five jiao. It is heard that the trend of fourteen yuan two jiao and two fen is still difficult to reverse.

Forming a Joint Company, yesterday was the second bidding period for Guangdong sugar in this city. The total quota was over ten thousand packages. The bid price was the same as before. It sold 740 packages of Shunde Factory’s Five Rams coarse white sugar at twenty-one yuan and two jiao, and 415 and 200 packages of the City New Factory at twenty yuan and seven jiao.

North-South Goods Longkou Vermicelli Customer Supply Insists 211

Recently, the sales of Longkou vermicelli have been slightly weak, and the market supply has slightly loosened. Yesterday (September 2nd), the higher-priced goods sold for twenty-five yuan, and the second-grade goods sold for twenty-four yuan and a half. However, the customer supply still insists and refuses to show weakness. High-quality goods are priced at twenty-one yuan, and the production price is still firm, showing signs that it is difficult to relax temporarily.

Hardware Ribbed Steel Bars Rise Again by More Than One Pound 212

Since the overseas price of ribbed steel bars has returned from five pounds twelve shillings to six pounds nine shillings, the local industry in this city has still been recklessly purchasing them, so the trading is extremely good. Yesterday, the overseas price suddenly rose to seven pounds eighteen shillings, which is one pound and nine shillings better than before. However, the industry believes that the price is too high and is afraid that it will be difficult to sell in the future, so most are taking a wait-and-see attitude, so the trading is slightly clearer than before. However, the market price in this city yesterday was as high as 160 yuan due to the soaring overseas prices. It is heard that there are only sporadic transactions.

John P. Holland (1841-1914) 213

— Zhang Shuying

— Inventor of the Submarine

The submarine is the most important weapon in modern scientific warfare. Its importance in war is equal to that of airplanes. We only need to look at the disputes over the increase, decrease, and abandonment of submarines in the major powers' disarmament conferences to understand how important the submarine is.

Given the current completeness of submarine equipment in various countries and the large number of submarines, some people must suspect that the invention of the submarine must have been very early and its history very long. In fact, the complete success of the submarine was only twenty or thirty years ago, that is, a few years before the European War. Even the initial research on submarines and the invention of manufacturing models were only a century ago. It is unbelievable that scientists have produced modern and very complete submarines after only a few decades of effort. Although submarines are weapons of war and disrupt world peace, the completeness of their creation and their great contribution to science are truly amazing. Therefore, we should not only understand the process of inventing submarines and the great men who invented them, but also admire them very much. Holland is such a person worthy of our admiration. With his patriotism and indomitable spirit, he finally succeeded despite several failures.

Holland was born in Ireland, England, in 1841. His family was well-off, and he received a full education from an early age. Later, he became a teacher at a monastery in Ireland. Whenever he had free time in the monastery, he devoted himself to researching submarines. At this time, the American Civil War happened to occur. He was greatly interested in and hopeful for the future when John Ericsson (1802-1880) built ironclad vehicles for the Northern Army to participate in the war and won the victory.

Holland's hope was for his homeland, Ireland, to break away from British rule and become a completely independent country. However, the British's powerful navy at the time was the biggest obstacle to achieving this. Now that Ericsson had invented ironclad warships, Ireland's independence could only become a dream with no hope of success. Since Holland had such a great hope to work for the independence of his country, the first thing he had to do was invent something that could contain the advance of the navy and was lower than ironclad warships. This was the biggest motivation for studying and manufacturing submarines. He thought that if submarines could dive into the water, they would definitely be able to break through enemy warships without the enemy's knowledge and win the war.

After Holland had this motivation to invent submarines, he devoted himself to studying the manufacture of submarines and the results of previous research. He learned from books that the first person to make a submarine model was the Dutchman Cornelis Von Prebbel (1742-1826); later, during the American Revolutionary War, the American Danid Bushnell (1742-1826) made a more complete submarine. This type of submarine only had one sailor, and it used manpower to dive into the water and could last for half an hour, but the experiment of attacking a British warship anchored in New York Harbor failed. It can be seen that the manufacturing was extremely simple and the mechanism was not perfect, so it could not be used.

The second person to study submarines was Robert Fulton (1765-1815), the inventor of the steamboat. He initially proposed to the US government to manufacture submarines, but it was not approved. Later, he proposed it abroad, but because he was not trusted, it did not attract people's attention or permission. However, he did not have the strength to manufacture it himself, so he gave up on submarines in disappointment.

Later, during the American Civil War, submarines were manufactured, and the Southern Army's submarine sank the Northern Army's battleship, but the structure was extremely simple and not very applicable.

Seeing that these predecessors had not achieved complete success in the manufacture and research of submarines, Holland was determined to become the person who completed the submarine. He went to the United States at the age of seventeen and landed in Boston. Unfortunately, this ambitious young man contracted a chronic illness soon after arriving in this new continent. The doctor wanted him to rest in the hospital for a long time. Unexpectedly, he got the opportunity to devote himself to studying submarines and came up with various methods for manufacturing submarines.

In 1875, when Holland was thirty-five years old, he initially made a very small submarine, but because the manufacturing was not yet complete, it was placed on the water and suddenly plunged into the mud, destroying the entire submarine. This submarine was cigar-shaped, sixteen feet long, and two feet wide in the center. The person sat in the center of the submarine and started the propulsion engine to move forward. It was named Holland No. 1. After the failure of No. 1, he was not discouraged and continued to manufacture No. 2, but because No. 2 was not improved, it followed the same path. After two failures, Holland had more and more experience. He was more confident that he would be able to complete this great mission, so he continued to work hard on research. Because he was engaged in Irish independence movement while researching, and the submarine he was researching was a tool to achieve the goal of independence, it was easy to obtain tens of thousands of dollars for his research, so he quickly manufactured two more submarines.

Holland's submarine was very different from those made by his predecessors. In the past, it took at least several minutes to completely flood, but Holland's could enter the depths of the water in just a few seconds and could move freely in the water. After Holland No. 3 and No. 4 were produced, he had achieved considerable success in his research on submarines. He then resigned from his teaching position and devoted all his efforts to researching more perfect submarines.

In 1888, Holland finally obtained the approval of the US Prime Minister to allow the US Navy to adopt submarines. Unfortunately, a political change in Washington occurred shortly after this permission, and it could not be implemented. By 1893, the US Department of the Navy accepted his opinion again and manufactured the Brandle submarine, but because the Washington government's technicians disagreed with some of Holland's designs, the ending was inevitably a failure. Holland was very angry and resentfully returned the government's nine thousand dollar price, took back the submarine, and then manufactured a new ship according to his own design, named "Holland." This Holland was the first modern submarine, 53 feet 10 inches long and 10 feet 7 inches deep. Shortly after this submarine was produced, war broke out between the United States and Spain, but the conservative US government was still unwilling to use the new weapon submarine as a tool to sink enemy ships.

In the fall of 1900, the US government gradually realized the great ability of submarines and began to buy the "Holland" submarine and ordered six similar Holland submarines from Holland. After a large exercise, the naval officers admired the power of the submarine very much. At this time, Holland had received great glory, and from then on, the navies of other countries also rushed to adopt submarines.

On September 22, 1914, a submarine sank several British battleships, which was exactly one month and ten days after the death of the great inventor of submarines, Holland.

Two Martyrs of Panmen 214

— Su Zihan

—Heroes Would Rather Die Than Be Humiliated—

Since the Jin army broke through Bianjing and captured Emperors Huizong and Qinzong, and established the great traitor Zhang Zongchang as emperor, the Song dynasty's empire was almost over. Fortunately, Emperor Gaozong escaped from the Jin camp, crossed the Yellow River, and ascended the throne in Nanjing. The loyalist troops and righteous men from all over the country arrived in Nanjing, and finally preserved the southern half of the empire.

Now that the foundation had been established, troops should have been mobilized to cross the Yellow River and fight the Jin army desperately to recover the lost territory and wash away the national shame. Unexpectedly, Gaozong did not do this, and listened to the words of ministers who only cared about enjoying wealth and glory and did not care about national affairs. He stayed in the south as emperor, and did not take the recovery of lost territory and the washing away of national shame seriously. As a result, the loyal and righteous Zong Ze, the garrison commander of Tokyo, was worried to death. When Commander Zong was dying, he still shouted "Cross the river!" It is a pity that Gaozong could not reuse such a bloody, courageous, loyal, and righteous minister.

Although Gaozong was enjoying himself in the south, the Jin army would never let him go. When the autumn was high and the grass was fat, and the people were strong and the horses were strong, they sent troops again, mighty and majestic, to kill south. At that time, among the generals guarding the Yellow River passes, there were two more traitors who betrayed the country for glory and surrendered the passes. Du Chong, Zong Ze's successor, was also a guy who only knew himself and did not know the country. Seeing the Jin army's power, he also surrendered. As a result, from the south of the Yellow River to the north bank of the Yangtze River, there was no place without Jin soldiers, and no place was not harassed by Jin soldiers.

At that time, Gaozong was in Pingjiang. Since the Jin army had come, he should have rushed to Nanjing to mobilize troops and generals to fight the Jin army. The Yangtze River was a natural barrier that the Jin army could not fly over even with wings. Even if they could not win, they could still defend it! Unfortunately, Gaozong did not do this, but listened to the words of useless guys like Huang Qianren and Wang Boyan. As soon as the Jin army broke through Yangzhou, he abandoned Pingjiang and ran madly to Hangzhou. Then he could not even defend Hangzhou and ran all the way to Mingzhou and entered the sea, which was considered to be settled.

In this way, the Jin army got what they wanted. Without any effort, they crossed the Yangtze River, broke through Nanjing, broke through Pingjiang, and followed Gaozong all the way to the sea before stopping. However, the people on the coast suffered a disaster. If Gaozong had not abandoned Pingjiang and relied on the natural barrier of the Yangtze River to fight the Jin army, the Jin army might not have gained an advantage, and might have even suffered a complete defeat.

Let's stop here. Although the officials were such failures, there were many ambitious, loyal, and righteous people among the common people who were unwilling to be slaves of a conquered country.

It is said that at that time, there were two common people in Pingjiang, one surnamed Liu, named Nain, and one surnamed Zhang, named Ao. These two friends were both from Bianjing. Because Bianjing was broken and Zhang Zongchang betrayed the country, his two friends were so angry that they had no power and could not do anything, so they had to complain to heaven and earth. Later, they heard that Gaozong had ascended the throne in Nanjing, and the two friends were extremely happy. They gathered together to discuss going to the south together. Fortunately, Zhang Ao had no family, and Liu Nai only had a wife, so it was not troublesome to leave.

After arriving in the south, Liu Nai and Zhang Ao settled in Pingjiang, and each found a small business to make a living.

After Gaozong arrived in Pingjiang, Pingjiang became lively and had a peaceful appearance. Everyone lived peacefully. Unexpectedly, the Jin army's ambition was not satisfied, and they raised troops again to seize the empire of China. The news became worse day by day, and everyone's good dreams were shattered.

When Liu Nai heard the news that the Jin army was coming again, he went to Zhang Ao and said, "I heard bad news that the Jin army is coming again, and they have crossed the Yellow River, broken through Bianjing, and Du Chong, that dog's bastard, has also surrendered! Brother, do you know?"

Zhang Ao replied, "Brother, I knew it long ago. This time, the emperor should send troops to fight the Jin army and defeat them completely. Not only should we take back Bianjing, but we should also take back the land north of the Yellow River to be worthy of the people and our ancestors!"

Liu Nai said, "That's hard to say. Think about it, Lord Yue is currently suppressing bandits in Huguang, and General Han and others are also in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River. What good generals does the emperor have around him? He only has those useless guys like Huang Qianren and Wang Boyan left. Do they have the courage to fight the Jin army desperately? Brother, what do you say?"

Zhang Ao said, "The emperor was able to escape from the Jin camp and run to the south alone to create a foundation. This courage and insight are not small. He should not run away as soon as he hears that the Jin army is coming, just like a mouse hears a cat meowing, without even seeing a shadow. Let's wait and see."

Liu Nai said, "Yes! Let's wait and see. Fortunately, my mind has long been made up. This life will sooner or later be spent fighting the Jin army."

Zhang Ao said, "Yes, it's natural to fight desperately when the time comes."

When the two friends had nothing to say, they parted.

After the Jin army broke through Yangzhou, the people of Pingjiang knew about the bad news, but they were still calm and not panicked at all. Originally, Yangzhou was still far from Pingjiang, and there was also a Yangtze River separating them! Unexpectedly, the officials could not calm down and slipped away to Hangzhou early.

Once the officials slipped away, it was really over. The people were all thinking, "Once the officials leave, it's clear that they don't want Pingjiang anymore, and the Jin army will naturally occupy Pingjiang. The Jin army is coming, what should we do?"

The streets were full of people, coming and going, panicking, all looking for friends and relatives, trying to discuss a good policy for the whole world.

Liu Nai also found Zhang Ao. As soon as they met, Liu Nai grabbed Zhang Ao's hand and shouted, "Brother, how was what I said? Those dog bastards are not fooling the emperor into running away, are they? They are really not something!"

Zhang Ao also shouted, "Such an emperor, he will run! He doesn't want the country, he doesn't want the land, he doesn't want the people, I really can't imagine it! Brother, now is the time!"

Liu Nai said: "That's right, now is the time, it's time for us to repay the country!"

Zhang Ao said, "However, brother, you have a sister-in-law!"

Liu Nai said, "Brother, don't say that, what time is it now, how can we care so much? Brother, your sister-in-law is also an understanding person. I said to her: 'For our country, for our nation, I am going to fight the Jin army. You are young, and you have no children. Take another step, don't remember me'! You opened your eyes and said: 'You can fight desperately. Don't squeeze me with words. Look at me.' Saying that, she turned around and left, ha! Brother, she wiped her neck and died! She died well! She is a good citizen of Great Song, and a good wife of my Liu Nai..."

Zhang Ao continued, "She is my Zhang Ao's good sister-in-law!"

Liu Nai said, "There must be more than just you and me who want to fight desperately, brother, let's go to the street and invite people!"

Zhang Ao said: "Good".

The two friends had already arrived on the street. The street was still so chaotic, and some were still carrying boxes and packages, preparing to escape.

Liu Nai shouted, "Don't go! You can't go!"

Someone replied: "If you don't go, are you waiting for the Jin army to come and cut off your head?"

Liu Nai shouted, "It's not like that, if you go, won't the Jin army follow? You still can't save your head. Now the officials don't want Pingjiang anymore, but we people want it, this is the land of Great Song! If we unite and fight the Jin army desperately, won't we protect Pingjiang and protect our families and wives and children? Don't go! Instead of dying if you leave, it's better to die happily fighting the Jin army!"

Zhang Ao also shouted, "It's the same as dying as a slave of a conquered country, it's also dying if you fight desperately, so it's more fun to die like this! Killing one person is enough, killing two people makes money!"

Shouting is shouting, but those who leave still leave. Let's stop here, is there really no one with hot blood? No, there are many people with hot blood. Look! Two or three hundred young people have jumped out of the crowd, shouting in unison: "Good man! I am willing to go with the two good men to fight the Jin army!"

Liu Nai shouted, "Good! We are people of Great Song when we are born, and ghosts of Great Song when we die. Let the Jin army taste the taste of our spear tips and knife heads."

Everyone also shouted: "Good! Heroes lead the way, we will find the Jin army to fight! Let's fight!"

A shout shook the heavens and the earth.

The Jin army came really fast.

After the Jin army broke through Yangzhou, they easily crossed the Yangtze River and captured Nanjing. No one resisted them along the way. They killed them mightily and majestically, and arrived in Pingjiang in a few days.

The Jin army had just arrived in Pingjiang, and there was still no news, when a team of warriors suddenly poured out of Panmen; at the head were Liu Nai and Zhang Ao. The two friends each held a death spear, and without saying a word, led the team of warriors into the Jin army's camp.

The Jin army was caught off guard and was disrupted by this team of mad tigers. Later, they realized that there were only a few people, so they surrounded them and fought. Liu Nai and Zhang Ao led everyone to charge left and right in the camp, killing so many people that corpses lay everywhere and blood flowed into rivers. The Jin army died a lot, but unfortunately, they were outnumbered. The people under their command gradually died, and Liu Nai also died in battle.

Seeing that the matter could not be successful, Zhang Ao thought: "Is it possible to have them take them away and be humiliated? It's better to die." Zhang Ao made up his mind, and while killing, he retreated, killing to the moat, and jumped into the moat and died.

The Jin army died thousands of people before they captured Pingjiang.

Afterwards, the people of Pingjiang admired the loyalty and righteousness of the two friends Liu Nai and Zhang Ao, and built a Shuangzhong Temple outside Lingyan Township in Panmen to commemorate them.

Publishing industry

"Educational Broadcasting Lecture Collection" 215

— Bin

Volume 1: Public Education

The first volume of "Educational Broadcasting Lecture Collection" (Public Education) and the volume of "Educational Broadcasting Lecture Collection" (Secondary Education) were edited by the Ministry of Education and published by The Commercial Press at the same time. The latter has already been introduced by the author, so here, let's just talk about the former. This collection is divided into four categories in terms of editing: Citizenship Training; Scientific Knowledge; Current Affairs Lectures; Mandarin Training. A total of twenty-nine speeches are included. First, let's talk about the allocation of materials. Judging from the amount of material in each category, this collection can be considered just right. The Citizenship Training category includes nine speeches, the Scientific Knowledge category includes fourteen speeches, the Current Affairs Lectures category includes five speeches, and the Mandarin Training category includes one speech: the allocation of materials is very appropriate in terms of emphasis.

However, in terms of the types of materials, this collection still has shortcomings and omissions. For example, in the Citizenship Training category, there is a type of training that is urgently needed at present, but it has not been included, and that is citizenship training during the national defense period. Any speeches that explain the environment and crisis our country is currently in can be included in the Current Affairs Lectures category; any speeches that explain the awareness and duties that citizens should have during the national defense period can be included in the Citizenship Training category; any speeches that introduce scientific knowledge related to national defense can be included in the Scientific Knowledge category. However, this collection has not paid attention to this aspect of the material. This, of course, cannot be the responsibility of the editors, but should be the responsibility of the organizers of the educational broadcasting lectures.

Also, for the Citizenship Training category, some articles about the cultivation of employment, career, and job seeking should be collected; for the Scientific Knowledge category, some lectures about common sense of classified occupations should be added. However, this collection has not paid attention to these materials. In addition, there are some necessary materials, such as lectures about public art education and training, that have not been noticed by this collection. In fact, this type of material has a very close relationship with public education. We can only hope that future educational broadcasting lectures will pay attention to the above-mentioned materials.

Secondly, let us give a general review of the quality of the materials in this collection. After we have read the twenty-nine speeches, we feel that none of them are knowledge that the public urgently needs. In particular, the nine speeches in the Citizenship Training category and the fourteen speeches in the Scientific Knowledge category are extremely detailed and clear in their analysis of truth and explanation of things. Speeches of this nature are, of course, easily understood by the general public.

Now, let's cite two speeches to discuss. For example, Xie Guansheng's speech on the rights and obligations of citizens can be said to be very accurate and detailed in its explanation of the topic. At the beginning of the speech, he explained the difference between citizens and people. Then, he clarified the conditions for being a citizen, that is: positive conditions; negative conditions; and under these two types of conditions, he listed several kinds. The next is the rights of citizens, including: private rights; public rights; and under these two types of rights, he listed several kinds. After that are the obligations of citizens, divided into: taxation; military service; education; obedience. Finally, he expressed this view in his conclusion: "In summary, only by meeting the conditions of a citizen, fulfilling obligations, and then enjoying various rights, can one be a complete and good citizen under the legal system of the Three Principles of the People." After listening to such a speech, the general public can understand their various relationships with the national government.

Another article we want to talk about is Chen Yunwei's speech on the benefits of the national calendar. Originally, topics such as calendars are quite difficult to explain, but she was able to explain it in a very detailed and popular way, which is a rare achievement. At the beginning of the speech, based on the two movements of the Earth, the causes of years, months, and days, and the influence of celestial phenomena on human life, she analyzed the definition of the national calendar very clearly. Then, she compared and explained the Chinese sexagenary cycle method of recording days and the foreign weekly method. Furthermore, she also talked about the four periods of the Chinese calendar, and listed the three disadvantages of the mixed Yin-Yang calendar. Then, she compared the composition methods of the old calendar and the national calendar; finally, she talked about the benefits of the national calendar. Regarding this point, she talked from the national calendar itself and social life, especially focusing on the latter. For such topics that the public urgently needs to know and are extremely difficult to explain, she explained them very carefully and easily understood in an organized way. Therefore, we consider this article to be the best of its kind.

In addition to the above-mentioned two speeches, there are some that are also very wonderful; such as: Chen Daqi's speech on Citizens and Morality, Zhang Lisheng's speech on Why China Should Implement the Three Principles of the People, and Zhang Yuzhe's speech on A Brief Introduction to the Universe. In short, educational broadcasting lectures are a powerful tool for emerging public education, and we hope that they will be held continuously in the future. At the same time, we also hope that the "Educational Broadcasting Lecture Collection" will continue to be edited, printed, and promoted, using the power of text to compensate for the shortcomings of broadcasting. However, in terms of the materials for broadcasting lectures, we hope that the organizers will do their best to expand them without any omissions.

Reading Guidance Second Series (Continued) 216

— Bin

——Published by The Commercial Press——

Third, let's discuss; Chen Zhima's How to Study Political Systems? At the beginning of the article, he explained several research methods for political systems, namely; philosophical, historical, comparative, and comprehensive methods. At the end of the article, he expressed his understanding of political systems; in detail, it is: ㈠ Political systems are one of the organizations of human society; ㈡ There is no absolute standard for the advantages and disadvantages of political systems; The method of taking the advantages of Chinese and Western political systems and discarding their disadvantages can never be realized. Such an understanding, especially the second and third points, can be said to be very insightful. Beginners who read this article will have a correct concept and understanding of political systems.

Fourth, it is Ruan Yicheng's How to Study Law? First, he explained the process of law changing from metaphysics to science; then, he clarified the scientific research methods of law. He abandoned the annotation research method of law and advocated the scientific research method: this is a transformation that legal scholars should have.

Fifth, let's talk about Zhong Luqi's How to Study Education? He divided the methods of studying education into two major categories: ordinary and special. Under the ordinary category, he further divided it into three points, namely: identifying categories; collecting materials; identifying reading materials. Under the special category, he further divided it into four points, namely: selecting appropriate questions; adopting appropriate methods; seeking sufficient evidence; composing accurate reports. His conclusion is this: "In short, to study education, one must be precise, erudite, practical, and use scientific methods to transform education into a true science." Zhong's method of studying education is the same as Ruan's method of studying law. In fact, the scientific method is the most appropriate method for modern people to study various academic disciplines.

Sixth, Jiang Wulifu's How to Study Western Literature. Like Ruan and Zhong, Wu also does not regard a certain academic discipline as isolated, but must relate it to other academic disciplines, especially social sciences. Therefore, when he talked about the basis of Western literature research methods, he listed "the perspective of social science" as the first item. Secondly, one must pay attention to the special position of China, which is the second item. The third item is that one should follow the needs of Chinese students. Due to these three reasons, he advocated that Chinese people should have their own research purposes and methods when studying Western literature, and there is no need to imitate people from other countries. He also opposed professors using European and American teaching methods to teach Western literature to Chinese students; or only paying attention to the value of foreign languages while ignoring the content of literature. In addition, he believes that the purpose of studying Western literature should be consistent with the method; that is, first determine a correct purpose, and then determine the research method. As for research opinions and preparations, he also has unique insights that can correct the errors of general Western literature scholars.

Other articles such as Yuan Daofeng's How to Study International Politics? and Chen Lijiang's How to Study Public Education? all have novel and correct explanations and appropriate research methods for the academic disciplines discussed. In short, the second series of Reading Guidance can be said to have done its best to guide readers in both materials and content. (End)

How to Study Philosophy (4) 217

— Yan Yilin

Authored by Wang Tefu, published by Sanjiang Bookstore

6. Critical Research of Philosophy:

In philosophical research, the critical research method has its broad needs; in order to correctly receive the legitimate philosophical heritage in history, in order to be able to scrape off all the crippled stagnation existing in the history of philosophy, in order to be able to recognize the theoretical system of all philosophical doctrines themselves, in order to be able to correctly evaluate the value of all philosophical thoughts, and even in order to be able to develop one's own philosophical thinking in research, obtain new knowledge and theories, establish one's own philosophical system, etc., all have their necessity, which is a very clear reason. However, how to conduct critical research? To understand a specific philosophy of an era and give a critical research to this philosophy, then one must first start from criticizing that era, first criticize and understand the real life of that era. In addition, one should also make a personal independent criticism of the identity and lifestyle of a certain philosopher in order to truly recognize and evaluate his philosophy. In this way, if we want to understand a philosophy, and to criticize this philosophy, then the main thing is to understand the philosopher's era background and class background, and to criticize that philosophy from the criticism of the era and class; secondly, it is to criticize his philosophy from the criticism of his personal life process. We should finally analyze out that certain parts of a certain philosophy can become a legitimate historical heritage and be received and become the content of philosophy, and use this to develop our own philosophical thoughts and form our own new philosophical system, which is considered the completion of the research work.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talk

High-Pitched Tune 218

— Li Sao

As the weather gets colder, the special scenes on the streets of Shanghai are not the colorful flags of discounted goods in fur shops, nor the smiling Santa Claus appearing in the windows, but the freezing and shivering expressions of the bums and beggars. To say that humans are not emotional animals is not necessarily true, because there are also people who are deeply moved by this expression, such as the establishment of soup kitchens and temporary shelters.

I am not very clear about the actual situation of these two institutions, but according to the records in the newspapers, they are obviously charitable in nature; no matter how short the period is, or how limited the accommodation is, they are much more beneficial to the poor than those who offer lip service but do not deliver.

However, in this society, there are only too many righteous people who sing high-pitched tunes. These righteous people always hide behind people's backs and even remain silent, but when something new appears, they become eloquent. Their words generally have a fixed formula. In addition to refuting you at the outset, they then launch into a tirade of complaints. As a result, praises such as "clear-headed" and "thoroughly resolved" are often attributed to them. But "clear-headed" is just clear-headed, and "thoroughly resolved" is just talking about it, and it's all right for others to be unlucky.

For example, shelters, etc., are of course not immune to their accusations. The first is that they should not be "temporary." Why should they be temporary? Do these poor people only need to be accommodated for these three months? After these three months, will they have a way to make a living? This is not thorough – The second is that there are too many poor people. Can such accommodation be as much as possible? If it cannot be as much as possible, then who should be excluded? This is not universal – But the responsibility of the righteous people seems to be only to shout out "not thorough" and "not universal." As for how to be universal and how to be thorough, that is "a long story," so I will "skip over it."

I am not against the thorough theory: I support thoroughness. However, I really don't dare to agree with the thoroughness of "high-pitched tunes" because its impact is that the shivering people are the ones who are going to be unlucky. As for themselves, after singing the high-pitched tune, they will immediately forget about it, because their main duty is to "sing," and "singing" is not limited to a certain event. When there is a need to "sing" in other areas, who can forbid them from singing loudly?

Under the current social system, there are reasons to criticize the establishment of temporary shelters and soup kitchens. However, the facts are in front of us. If we only sing "high-pitched tunes," even the few refugees who are accommodated during this short period will suffer a serious blow. Rather than watching them freeze and starve to death under the high-pitched tunes, it is not a crime to let them drink a bowl of thin porridge and sleep on some straw. However, the inherent habits of the Chinese people cannot be ignored, and that is the issue of the integrity of the handlers. Judging from the cases impeached by the Control Yuan, we know that even some officials are suspected of corruption, let alone charitable organizations – precisely because they are charitable, as long as one person manipulates things, the stomachs of many people will suffer. Therefore, under the current situation, at the very least, we require them to make their accounts public. On the one hand, it can gain the trust of the true philanthropists who donate money, and on the other hand, it can ensure the treatment that the disaster victims can enjoy. But this kind of shouting seems to be far from high-pitched tunes!

Page 20

Light Snow 219

— Luo Yu

One early winter, I lived in the slum district of Nantao, T City. One cold night, I passed through the concession, dazzling with bicycle bells and neon lights, and walked onto the black, garbage-covered hills. The first thing that shocked me was a frozen, naked body, a dark, fleshly figure abandoned by the roadside like a fallen, withered tree.

There were no pedestrians within three hundred meters, only a ditch filled with black skirmish lines, lying ugly across the road. Surrounded by the cold, I felt a chill down my spine and hurriedly escaped across the small plank bridge to find those familiar young people.

Later, I heard that most of those corpses were opium addicts. They could go without food or lodging, inject morphine and sleep in dog kennels out in the winter night. They were originally not worthy of our pity.

The dockworkers in the slum district, even if they were hungry, still tried to find a place to stay. In the evening, they clutched a handful of copper coins and walked silently into the small shops. Those who stayed there were still their usual companions, inquiring about each other before sleeping on a wooden bunk. They could avoid thinking about those who were knocked down by the wind and snow.

One morning, I got up and went out at five or six o'clock. The sky was still gloomy, and the light snow of the night was still falling quietly. The snow on the ground was very thin, and it had not yet covered the remaining warmth of early winter, like white sugar placed on yellow rice cake, melting with the light steam. I was wearing a simple worker's outfit, which, though old and worn, was able to keep out the cold. Moreover, the habitual sound sleep had given me an overflowing life, so I went to the pier without hesitation.

When I reached the corner at the end of the small cross alley, I saw a living person sleeping on his back on the wet, melting snow. I was used to seeing this, but his clothes caught my attention. The clothes were neat, a black cotton robe and an old cloth vest. The robe above his knees was covered with a layer of melting snow. His hands were half-clenched, like a racing athlete.

I observed this life fighting against the cold with great composure. They were indeed fighting each other physically. He looked only about twenty years old, with his eyes closed, showing the red flesh of his eyelids, which looked very scary. The melting snow on his face was like a small snake winding around the roots of his ears, gradually killing this wandering young man. White foam was bubbling from his mouth, spitting out curse-like dental sounds.

When I looked up, I saw a middle-aged, hunched person at the entrance of the alley, as if urinating. He went around and went into a small shop. I wondered if this person was trying to steal the wanderer's clothes, which was a common occurrence, and no one would see it in this situation. On the ground were indistinguishable footprints, a layer of black mud, and a thin layer of snow.

Such an impression could no longer move me. I only thought: this wanderer may not be one of those opium addicts. Looking at his clothes, he is a countryman, not like someone who has been mixing with urban coolies for a long time. While thinking, I had already reached the road in the concession.

Far away, a tram drove past, emitting a clear, cold bell sound. There was not a single life on the street. Between the branches of the parallel rows of street trees was stacked unmelted snow. I stomped across the asphalt road, and at this time only a few workers were heading towards the river bank.

Suddenly, something seemed to explode in my brain, causing me to stop. I thought of the corpse I had encountered that night, and the broken house I had been to that night. It was a low earthen house, with light shining through the window paper. When I squeezed in, it was warm inside. Three young people were close to an old coal stove on the edge of the bunk, and a pair of smelly, broken boots were placed next to the stove. Their clothes were very thin. Another person was squatting on the bunk, covering himself with a torn quilt, only showing his face. Behind the half partition was another room, with several men huddling together to gamble, and from time to time there was a dull noise.

I remember that the young man covering himself with the quilt didn't talk much. But I knew he had run away from a village not far from T City. His protruding forehead clearly marked his rurality, and his eyes were vaguely suspicious. This is what made me recall with surprise and stop.

I hurried back, following the original road, wanting to save the poor fellow. I could no longer remember his name, but his face vividly poured into my brain.

The snow was still falling. I walked very fast, but I hoped in my heart that it was just a stranger, because the death of a stranger was something I was used to seeing. But with the damp footsteps, my heart was beating.

I had already turned into the small cross alley. When I reached the corner, under a mud wall, a withered body lay crooked in the muddy water. His face was covered with a lot of mud, but the most terrible thing was the protruding skull that I was familiar with. He had already stopped struggling and allowed the snowflakes to slowly sprinkle on his skin.

On the thin snow, there was still a row of footprints that were about to disappear, stepping towards the small shop at the entrance of the alley. Beside the person swallowed by the snow, there was only a pair of old boots placed on the snow, one of which was a pair of quite old boots that I had seen by a stove.

Mountain Sedan 220

— Luo

The so-called mountain sedan is just a rattan chair with two bamboo poles. Most people who go to Hangzhou to burn incense have had the experience of riding this kind of rattan sedan. However, the reason why mountain sedans are so simplified is to make it easier for the sedan bearers to climb the mountain, and also to reduce the danger for those riding in the sedan. People who are confined to the city already have a sense of fear when they see the mountains in Hangzhou. Going from Lingyin to Beigaofeng, there is a section of mountain road that is very narrow. People who climb the mountain on foot don't feel any danger because they only pay attention to the mountain road at their feet. Although those riding in the sedan can save their energy and leisurely smoke cigarettes in the sedan, looking around and enjoying the narrow Qiantang River like a jade belt, or the houses that are vaguely visible; but precisely because of this leisure, when they accidentally shift their gaze to the mountain road below the sedan, it feels like flying in the air. At the turning points, it is even more like the sedan body is about to fall down immediately, but the four legs of the sedan bearers in front and behind are moving firmly. They are stepping firmly on the stone steps, cautiously and quickly, wanting to reach the peak as soon as possible. They can also sit down on the stone railings in front of the temple to rest for a while, or even have a cup of cool tea to drink. People riding in the sedan often don't think this way, and they even forget the only merit of coming to Hangzhou—burning incense. When their eyes are closer and closer, they all think that the sedan bearers' legs may accidentally step on empty air, causing them to fall from the mountainside with the sedan and be smashed to pieces. Timid grandmothers and wives prefer to run out of the sedan and support themselves with climbing sticks, slowly climbing a section of road, letting the mountain sedan follow behind. Sure enough, their excuses are very beautiful: "Burning incense requires sincerity, it is best to climb all the way from the foot of the mountain to the top." Seeing the Mao Shan Taoists sitting cross-legged on the corner of the mountain, they are giving alms to the incense without missing one. But after climbing a section of the road, they also think that since they have already spent money to hire a mountain sedan, it is a bit wasteful to climb the mountain with effort, and besides, the grandmothers and wives who feel pain in the soles of their feet when walking on flat ground. Their thoughts turned again, they took a long-distance train to burn incense, and it can't be said that sitting in a mountain sedan on the mountain isn't sincere and pious. The Bodhisattva can forgive them. But when they sat back in the sedan, the mountain was even higher, and they were worried that the sedan bearers' legs would step on empty air. A wife once told me that her psychological analysis when she went up the mountain to burn incense may also be the climbing psychology of general grandmothers and wives? I have also climbed the mountains in Hangzhou, but I have never ridden in a mountain sedan, and I don't know how I would panic when sitting in a mountain sedan? This time I traveled to Huangshan, I rode in a mountain sedan. Comparing Huangshan to the peaks of Hangzhou is truly incomparable; but using the psychology of sitting in a Huangshan mountain sedan to infer the psychology of sitting in a Hangzhou mountain sedan can be seen in general. I can't describe the scenery of Huangshan, sitting in the sedan, my eyes didn't have free time to peep at the sedan bearers' legs. The mountain road is probably narrower and more straight, and the sedan bearers often carry the bamboo poles in their hands instead of shouldering them. At the turning points, the sedan bearers in front lift the bamboo poles, while the sedan bearers in the back raise them above their heads. It looks like the sedan is attached

Huangpu Riverbank 221

— By Ma Mengchen

Page 21

As if standing on solid ground, even if I were overlooking a deep abyss, I would never have thought of becoming a ghost in a foreign land along with the sedan chair. Because I wanted to test my courage, I had been staring at the legs of the sedan carriers, but they moved so fast that I couldn't even see the mountain road clearly, making me feel like I was riding the clouds. In that case, when the person and the sedan chair tumble down, I probably wouldn't think about the danger after falling, but only see the mountain spinning before my eyes. I have never flown in an airplane, but based on this experience of riding a mountain sedan chair, it seems that even if I have the opportunity to fly in an airplane, I would never think about how the poet Xu Zhimo died.

Medicine 222

Common Knowledge of Tuberculosis Prevention

Dunben (800) 7:15 PM to 8:00 PM

The harm of tuberculosis is more cruel than guns and cannons, but people have not paid attention to it. They do not know the methods of prevention, nor do they know the importance of early diagnosis. As a result, they delay and make mistakes, and are eventually killed by tuberculosis bacteria (i.e., tubercle bacilli). What a pity!

The rampant spread of tuberculosis in our country is truly terrifying. The number of people who die from this disease each year is as high as 1.4 million, and the number of people suffering from tuberculosis is 27 million (an average of six out of every hundred people, and one out of every sixteen people suffer from tuberculosis). If calculated by time, three people die from tuberculosis every minute. Just imagine how significant this loss of talent and economy is! Moreover, most of those who die from tuberculosis are young people. They are the productive forces of society, and they are giving their all, but just when they are about to achieve something, they are swallowed up by tuberculosis. What a pity!

Opening Passage: "Busy with Socializing"

The romantic affairs are lively and unrestrained. Celebrations and funerals involve a lot of expenses. Zhao, Qian, Sun, Li, Zhou, Wu, Zheng. One-cent stamps fly all over the sky. Unobstructed passage in all directions. Friendships exist everywhere. Spring breeze and summer rain naturally correspond. However, families in the mainland are already afraid of the bitterness of socializing. That taste in Shanghai is even more difficult to bear. When a child is one month or one year old. Sending out invitation cards, what harm is there? The lady of the house, twenty or thirty years old. A grand banquet celebrates a magnificent hall. The person himself adds even more excitement. Small banquets are common on birthdays. Also, every family has ancestral halls. Not willing to forget the morning and evening sacrifices. Filial sons and virtuous grandchildren are praised by everyone. Red envelopes are written with incense. If they could know in the dark. They would smile happily in the underworld. The anniversary of the burial is calculated separately. Plus entering the ancestral hall. The four seasons revolve in a circle. Red and white posts are really like urging grain. It's all because, Golden Hairpin throwing herself into the well hurt Shen Ying.

Movies

"Female Classmates" Will be Released in All Theaters 226

The most popular production of Tianyi Film Company, "Female Classmates", is a sound epic about the romance of male and female classmates. The beautiful rising star Chen Qixia plays a smart, lively, and utterly childish female student. Her acting skills have achieved even more rapid progress than in "Huangpu Riverbank". Fan Xuepeng and the new popular young actor Tao Jin co-star. Jiang Jingcheng, Liang Lvyuan, Leng Bo, Wang Huijuan, Xiao Zhengzhong, Shen Yalan, Li Lin, Ning Xuan, and others also play important roles. The play aims to promote the spirit of mutual help among classmates and guide young people on the right path in life. It not only contains educational significance but is also full of dramatic interest. The depth of expression is especially thought-provoking. It is now scheduled to be released at the Jincheng Grand Theater starting on the 18th of this month (Friday), it is said.

Hu Die Murders 227

—In "Eternal Smile"—

In Wu Village's "Eternal Smile".

Hu Die, to raise the last hundred yuan for her lover Gong Jianong, was threatened by money to satisfy the animal desires of a pawnshop owner, Cheng Zhao, with her body and obtain one hundred yuan. Her exhausted body walked out of the pawnshop in the storm. Unexpectedly, her uncle Luo Kuang robbed her of the money she had obtained in that way. She cried, she shouted, but to no avail. She had to enter Cheng Zhao's bedroom for the second time. Cheng Zhao was filing his nails, and since he no longer desired her, he had become cruel and terrible. She was furious and made vicious accusations, and she had a big fight with him. She was pressed on the table, but her hand touched the scissors. She grabbed the scissors and stabbed them into Cheng Zhao's waist, one stab, two stabs. Cheng Zhao made a final struggling sound and fell to the ground dead. Hu Die trembled in great horror, widened her eyes and looked at the blood on her hands. Soon, she calmed herself slightly, quickly washed the bloody hands, quickly robbed the deceased's treasury, and quickly fled.

Soon, on a stormy night, the city guard caught a woman dressed as a man, and she was Hu Die. This sensational murderer was thus arrested.

Random Chatter 228

The "Thunder and Lightning Drama Society", which has been established for more than a year, has planned several performances, but they have all been aborted due to script issues. Recently, they have been actively rehearsing the two plays "Children Without a Motherland" and "The Proposal". The director is Zuo Ming, and it is expected that they will be performed at the end of this month.

It is rumored that the No. 2 Studio of Star Film Company recently planned to borrow the basic actor Zhou Xuan from Yihua Film Company to film a movie. It is said that all the conditions have been agreed upon. According to officials of Yihua Film Company, it is true that there is a matter of borrowing Zhou Xuan, but it is absolutely not negotiated, and all the procedures are still in contact.

Lianhua's "Orphan Girl Martyr Girl" will be released exclusively at the Xinguang Theater starting on the 19th. The Carlton is probably going to be replaced by the Chinese Traveling Theater Troupe.
